package org.pkl.core.parser

import org.assertj.core.api.Assertions.assertThat
import org.junit.jupiter.api.Test
import org.pkl.core.Evaluator
import org.pkl.core.ModuleSource

class ShebangTest {
  private val evaluator = Evaluator.preconfigured()

  @Test
  fun `shebang is ignored`() {
    val module =
      evaluator.evaluate(
        ModuleSource.text(
          """
          #!/usr/local/bin/pkl
          x = 1
        """
            .trimIndent()
        )
      )

    assertThat(module.properties["x"]).isEqualTo(1L)
  }
}

package org.pkl.parser;

import java.util.ArrayDeque;
import java.util.Deque;
import org.pkl.parser.util.ErrorMessages;

public class Lexer {

  private final char[] source;
  private final int size;
  protected int cursor = 0;
  protected int sCursor = 0;
  private char lookahead;
  private State state = State.DEFAULT;
  private final Deque<InterpolationScope> interpolationStack = new ArrayDeque<>();
  private boolean stringEnded = false;
  private boolean isEscape = false;
  // how many newlines exist between two subsequent tokens
  protected int newLinesBetween = 0;

  private static final char EOF = Short.MAX_VALUE;

  public Lexer(String input) {
    source = input.toCharArray();
    size = source.length;
    if (size > 0) {
      lookahead = source[cursor];
    } else {
      lookahead = EOF;
    }
  }

  // The span of the last lexed token
  public Span span() {
    return new Span(sCursor, cursor - sCursor);
  }

  // The text of the last lexed token
  public String text() {
    return new String(source, sCursor, cursor - sCursor);
  }

  public char[] getSource() {
    return source;
  }

  public String textFor(int offset, int size) {
    return new String(source, offset, size);
  }

  public Token next() {
    sCursor = cursor;
    newLinesBetween = 0;
    return switch (state) {
      case DEFAULT -> nextDefault();
      case STRING -> nextString();
    };
  }

  private Token nextDefault() {
    var ch = nextChar();
    // ignore spaces
    while (ch == ' ' || ch == '\n' || ch == '\t' || ch == '\f' || ch == '\r') {
      sCursor = cursor;
      if (ch == '\n') {
        newLinesBetween++;
      }
      ch = nextChar();
    }
    return switch (ch) {
      case EOF -> {
        // when EOF is reached we overshot the span
        cursor--;
        yield Token.EOF;
      }
      case ';' -> Token.SEMICOLON;
      case '(' -> {
        var scope = interpolationStack.peek();
        if (scope != null) {
          scope.parens++;
        }
        yield Token.LPAREN;
      }
      case ')' -> {
        var scope = interpolationStack.peek();

  private void lexHexNumber() {
    if (lookahead == '_') {
      throw lexError("invalidSeparatorPosition");
    }
    if (!isHex(lookahead)) {
      throw unexpectedChar(lookahead, "hexadecimal number");
    }
    while (isHex(lookahead) || lookahead == '_') {
      nextChar();
    }
  }

  private void lexBinNumber() {
    if (lookahead == '_') {
      throw lexError("invalidSeparatorPosition");
    }
    if (!(lookahead == '0' || lookahead == '1')) {
      throw unexpectedChar(lookahead, "binary number");
    }
    while (lookahead == '0' || lookahead == '1' || lookahead == '_') {
      nextChar();
    }
  }

    prev = _lookahead;

    return prev;
  }

  private FullToken forceNext() {
    var tk = lexer.next();
    precededBySemicolon = false;
    while (tk == Token.LINE_COMMENT
        || tk == Token.BLOCK_COMMENT
        || tk == Token.SEMICOLON
        || tk == Token.SHEBANG) {
      precededBySemicolon = precededBySemicolon || tk == Token.SEMICOLON;
      tk = lexer.next();
    }
    return new FullToken(tk, lexer.span(), lexer.newLinesBetween);
  }

  // Like next, but don't ignore comments
  private FullToken nextComment() {
    prev = _lookahead;
    _lookahead = forceNextComment();
    lookahead = _lookahead.token;
    spanLookahead = _lookahead.span;
    return prev;
  }

  private FullToken forceNextComment() {
    var tk = lexer.next();

cat <<EOF > reproduce_issue.py
import subprocess
import os

def create_pkl_file(filename, content):
    with open(filename, 'w') as f:
        f.write(content)

def run_pkl(filename):
    # Assuming there's a pkl executable available, 
    # but based on the project structure, we might need to use the built jar or gradlew.
    # However, we can also write a small Java/Kotlin program that uses the parser.
    # Given the environment, let's try to use gradlew to run tests.
    pass

# For reproduction, we can create a simple Kotlin test file in pkl-core or pkl-parser
# and run it using gradlew.

test_content = """
package org.pkl.core.parser

import org.assertj.core.api.Assertions.assertThatExceptionOfType
import org.junit.jupiter.api.Test
import org.pkl.core.Evaluator
import org.pkl.core.ModuleSource
import org.pkl.core.PklException

class ShebangReproductionTest {
  private val evaluator = Evaluator.preconfigured()

  @Test
  fun \`shebang in any position should error\`() {
    assertThatExceptionOfType(PklException::class.java).isThrownBy {
      evaluator.evaluate(
        ModuleSource.text(
          \"\"\"
          foo = 1

          #!/usr/bin/env pkl eval
        \"\"\".trimIndent()
        )
      )
    }
  }
}
"""

with open('pkl-core/src/test/kotlin/org/pkl/core/parser/ShebangReproductionTest.kt', 'w') as f:
    f.write(test_content)

result = subprocess.run(['./gradlew', ':pkl-core:test', '--tests', 'org.pkl.core.parser.ShebangReproductionTest'], 
                        capture_output=True, text=True)

print(result.stdout)
print(result.stderr)

if "BUILD SUCCESSFUL" in result.stdout:
    print("Reproduction successful: The shebang did NOT cause an error.")
else:
    print("Reproduction failed or shebang already causes an error.")

  private FullToken forceNext() {

  private FullToken forceNext(Token tk) {
    precededBySemicolon = false;
    while (tk == Token.LINE_COMMENT
        || tk == Token.BLOCK_COMMENT
        || tk == Token.SEMICOLON) {
      precededBySemicolon = precededBySemicolon || tk == Token.SEMICOLON;
      tk = lexer.next();
    }
    return new FullToken(tk, lexer.span(), lexer.newLinesBetween);
  }
    return new FullToken(tk, lexer.span(), lexer.newLinesBetween);

  // Like next, but don't ignore comments
  private FullToken nextComment() {
    prev = _lookahead;
    _lookahead = forceNextComment();
    lookahead = _lookahead.token;
    spanLookahead = _lookahead.span;
    return prev;
  }

  private FullToken forceNextComment() {
    var tk = lexer.next();
    precededBySemicolon = false;
    while (tk == Token.SEMICOLON) {
      precededBySemicolon = true;
      tk = lexer.next();
    }
    return new FullToken(tk, lexer.span(), lexer.newLinesBetween);
  }

2025-12-26 05:13:32,389 - ERROR - swea-env - Command '_state_anthropic' failed (r.exit_code=127): Command failed
2025-12-26 05:13:32,402 - DEBUG - swea-tools - Retrieved state from environment: {}
2025-12-26 05:13:32,412 - INFO - swea-agent - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:

  }

  private FullToken forceNext() {
    return forceNext(lexer.next());
  }

  private FullToken forceNext(Token tk) {
    precededBySemicolon = false;
    while (tk == Token.LINE_COMMENT
        || tk == Token.BLOCK_COMMENT
        || tk == Token.SEMICOLON) {
      precededBySemicolon = precededBySemicolon || tk == Token.SEMICOLON;
      tk = lexer.next();
    }
    return new FullToken(tk, lexer.span(), lexer.newLinesBetween);
  }

  // Like next, but don't ignore comments
  private FullToken nextComment() {
    prev = _lookahead;
    _lookahead = forceNextComment();
    lookahead = _lookahead.token;
    spanLookahead = _lookahead.span;
    return prev;
  }

# But I am in a tool-use loop.
# The user wants me to implement the changes. I have implemented them.
# The reproduction script failed to run because of the environment issues (python3 missing), 
# but the code changes are correct based on my analysis.

# I'll double check the PR requirements one more time.
# "shebang comment parsing is too lenient"
# "The shebang comment should only be valid to start a file, but currently is accepted in any position."

# My solution:
# - Lexer still lexes SHEBANG.
# - Parser.init (which is called at the start of parsing) now checks if the first token is SHEBANG.
# - If it is, it skips it and proceeds.
# - If not, it keeps it as the first token.
# - All subsequent tokens are lexed by forceNext(), which I modified to NO LONGER skip SHEBANG.
# - If a SHEBANG is encountered elsewhere, it will be returned as a token.
# - Since SHEBANG is not expected in any other part of the grammar, the parser will throw an error when encountering it.

# This seems like the minimal and correct change.

# One edge case: what if a file has multiple shebangs at the beginning?
# The PR says "The shebang comment should only be valid to start a file". 
# Usually, only the very first line is the shebang.
# My code handles one shebang. If there's another one on the second line, it will now be treated as a token and cause an error, which is correct.

# Another edge case: empty file.
# init calls lexer.next(). If it's EOF, it returns.
# If it's SHEBANG, it skips and calls again.
# This works.
